Unfortunately, celebrations will have to happen virtually this year because of the COVID-19 pandemic. of anxiety for children even at the best of times, whether they&#8217;re dealing with illness themselves, have friends or family members who are ill, or are just beginning to learn that while their bodies are amazing tools, they sometimes need a bit of care. An anatomy book and a colouring book all in one, this book will show your child how their body works and encourage their creativity at the same time.  </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0746041179/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0746041179\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"Buy from Amazon\" data-title=\"Going to the Doctor (Usborne First Experiences)\" data-publisher=\"Usborne Pub Ltd\" data-releasedate=\"2001-12-01\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Usborne First Experiences: Going to the Doctor</a> by Anne Civardi    </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Visiting the doctor can be an intimidating experience whatever your age, but when you&#8217;re very young, it can be genuinely frightening. Civardi&#8217;s book shows small children that getting a checkup doesn&#8217;t have to be scary and gives them an idea of what to expect during their trip. And as it&#8217;s an Usborne book, you can try to spot the yellow duck on every page as you read together. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0794533116/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0794533116\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"Buy from Amazon\" data-title=\"Look Inside Your Body;Look Inside Board Books\" data-publisher=\"Usborne Books\" data-releasedate=\"2013-01-01\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Usborne Look Inside Your Body</a> by Louie Stowell  </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>This lift-the-flap book is another great resource for teaching your child about anatomy, showing how different bodily processes (breathing, digesting, using your brain) happen in a way simple enough for even very young children to understand. This lighthearted book will help your child learn about themselves without making it too serious—and kids who love toilet humour will be very happy. </p></div></div></div>\n<div However, when she starts a new school, Kayla becomes anxious about managing her condition, and how her new friends will react when they learn about her illness. <em>I&#8217;m No Different Than You</em> is a great way to learn about sickle cell anaemia, with a loveable and determined heroine. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0648085910/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0648085910\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"Buy from Amazon\" data-title=\"My Strong Mind: A Story About Developing Mental Strength (Positive Mindset series)\" data-publisher=\"Truebridges Media\" data-releasedate=\"2017-10-20\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">My Strong Mind</a> by Niels Van Hove</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Health issues can often have an impact on mental health, and many children deal with mental illness. <em>My Strong Mind</em> contains kid-friendly tips on developing resilience and dealing with everyday stress or more acute incidents of anxiety. As well as working through techniques like mindfulness and self-acceptance, this book encourages kids and their guardians to talk about mental health.</p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1434397203/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1434397203\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/chemo-to-the-rescue.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"Chemo to the Rescue cover\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1434397203/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1434397203\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"Buy from Amazon\" data-title=\"Chemo to the Rescue: A Children's Book About Leukemia\" data-publisher=\"AuthorHouse\" data-releasedate=\"2008-10-27\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Chemo to the Rescue</a> by Caitlin Knutsson and Mary Brent</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Co-authored by child leukemia survivor Caitlin, this picture book is a reassuring introduction to this common childhood illness, and the ways it&#8217;s treated— including chemo. <em>Chemo to the Rescue</em> is another helpful read for children who are facing treatment themselves, or who know someone who is. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0982993803/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0982993803\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"Buy from Amazon\" data-title=\"Your Fantastic Elastic Brain: Stretch It, Shape It\" data-publisher=\"Little Pickle Press\" data-releasedate=\"2010-12-13\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Your Fantastic Elastic Brain</a> by JoAnn Deak </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>The brain is sometimes overlooked in medical books for kids, but <em>Your Fantastic Elastic Brain</em> redresses that balance. The book doesn&#8217;t just teach you how your brain works—it also delves into tips and tricks that children can use to take control of their brains. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00HTK9MCQ/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=B00HTK9MCQ\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"By Dorling Kindersley - Dk First Human Body Encyclopedia\" data-publisher=\"Dorling Kindersley Ltd.\" data-releasedate=\"2004-12-26\" class=\"butter\">First Human Body Encyclopedia</a> by Dorling Kindersley  </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>If you&#8217;ve got a budding biologist, this comprehensive encyclopaedia by educational titan Dorling Kindersley is the perfect gift. With beautiful, clear illustrations, this book will help your child learn about all the different systems of the human body and how they work together. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/bray-bray.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><em><a href=\"https://globalhealth.emory.edu/_includes/documents/sections/ebook-competition/bray_bray_conquers_the_coronavirus.pdf\">Bray Bray Conquers the Coronavirus</a></em> by Ashley Maxie-Moreman and Joanah Whitely</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>COVID-19 is a topic that many children (and everyone else) may find confusing and frightening. Luckily, this book gives a clear explanation of what the coronavirus is, the best ways to stay safe from infection, and also helps children deal with their feelings as they process the new normal. (At the time of writing, this book is available free from Emory Global Health Institute).</p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><em><a href=\"https://globalhealth.emory.edu/_includes/documents/sections/ebook-competition/goingtobeok.pdf\">We&#8217;re Going to be OK</a></em> by Ebony Jade Hilton</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Another great COVID resource, this book is aimed at helping children manage their stress about the virus, especially children from vulnerable groups. A medical doctor herself, author Ebony Jade Hilton has created a book that will help children of frontline workers, particularly from Black and POC communities. (At the time this post was published, this book was available for free from Emory Global Health Institute).</p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0578425165/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0578425165\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"Buy from Amazon\" data-title=\"Cell Biology For Babies\" data-publisher=\"Haitham Ahmed Publishing\" data-releasedate=\"2019-01-01\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Cell Biology for Babies</a> by Haitham Ahmed  </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Getting right down to the basics of anatomy, this book explains cells in a way that even very small children can understand. With clear illustrations and explanations, this is also a useful primer for any parents who want to brush up on their cell biology! </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/055255166X/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=055255166X\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/pig-heart.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/055255166X/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=055255166X\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"Buy from Amazon\" data-title=\"Pig Heart Boy\" data-publisher=\"CORGI CHILDRENS\" data-releasedate=\"2004T\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Pig-Heart Boy</a> by Malorie Blackman  </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Delving a little into sci-fi (but the kind of sci-fi that&#8217;s very close to becoming a reality), this classic book by Malorie Blackman follows the story of Cameron, a boy with a serious heart condition who&#8217;s offered a groundbreaking new treatment: a heart transplant from a genetically engineered pig. Looking at medical ethics as well as medical treatment, this is a great medical read for older kids. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a product-id=\"1409562905\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1409562905/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1409562905\" target=\"_blank\" butter=\"butter\" nofollow=\"nofollow\" title=\"Buy from Amazon\" data-title=\"How Your Body Works\" data-publisher=\"Usborne Publishing Ltd\" data-releasedate=\"2013-10-01\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">How Your Body Works</a> by Judy Hindley</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>&#8220;Recommend&#8221; is a strong word for this book, but it deserves a special mention for being educational and yet utterly bizarre. As a child growing up in the late &#8217;80s, this book taught me how bodies fight off pathogens by depicting the human body as a castle guarded by white blood cell knights, a useful metaphor. It taught me the way digestion worked by showing an eating, digesting, and excreting machine. And it had a page about sex ed…featuring large, industrial-equipment-looking robots. That last part didn&#8217;t illuminate so much as thoroughly confuse, so while your kid will probably need a few extra explanations after reading this one, it&#8217;s good for a giggle. </p></div></div></div>\n<hr class=\"wp-block-separator\"/>\n<p>To help your kids broaden their knowledge even further, check out our list of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\"25 of the Best Children's Books About Health and Safety (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://bookriot.com/childrens-books-about-health\" target=\"_blank\">25 of the Best Children&#8217;s Books About Health and Safety</a>. If building up your children&#8217;s booklist has piqued your own interest in medicine, we have <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\"50 Books to Read if you Love Medicine (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://bookriot.com/50-books-to-read-if-you-love-medicine\" target=\"_blank\">plenty of options for adults, too</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a -039_a6b73288b3c3031b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/bookriot/WlRy?d=ZC7T4KBF6Nw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn43@2020_6/2020/08/31/08-19-44-555_f5d09097629b39ce.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/bookriot/WlRy?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn11@2020_1/2020/08/31/08-19-44-808_6356ad1b69a203e9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/bookriot/WlRy/~4/NACp8jlZeN8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn3@2020_6/2020/08/31/08-19-43-482_63b68b05d5713982.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598861981420},{"createdTime":"2020-08-31 16:19:41","updatedTime":"2020-08-31 16:19:41","title":"Books For Dummies: A Key to Information","link":"https://bookriot.com/?p=444211","description":"\n<p>Browsing a bookstore in the mid-&#8217;90s, a particular black and yellow spine really stood out in the stacks. The striking colors caught the eye, making the browser wonder what this book for dummies could teach them.&#160; </p>\n<p>The <em>For Dummies</em> books really found popularity during the height of the dot-com bubble halfway through the decade. Laypeople with no knowledge of computer technology were seeking out easily-digestible information about software, coding, and operating systems. While working for Bantam Doubleday Dell publishers in New York, IDG Books co-founder and CEO John Kilcullen overheard a computer software store customer lamenting his need for an easy-to-follow book about computers. Unknowingly titling their very first book, this customer said he was looking for &#8220;Something like DOS for Dummies&#8221;, and hence an entire series was born. Published by Kilcullen&#8217;s IDG Books, <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" product-id=\"0764503618\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0764503618/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0764503618\" target=\"_blank\" butter=\"butter\" nofollow=\"nofollow\" data-title=\"DOS For Dummies\" data-publisher=\"For Dummies\" data-releasedate=\"1998-06-02\" class=\"butter\">DOS for Dummies</a> was written by Dan Gookin. His writing in DOS went on to inform the voice of the entire series, incorporating humor into these books designed to engage and educated novices. He would go on to write seven more books for the <em>Dummies</em> franchise, his last one to-date titled <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" product-id=\"1119453852\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1119453852/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1119453852\" target=\"_blank\" butter=\"butter\" nofollow=\"nofollow\" data-title=\"Android Phones &#38; Tablets For Dummies (For Dummies (Computer/Tech))\" data-publisher=\"For Dummies\" data-releasedate=\"2017-12-26\" class=\"butter\">Android Tablets For Dummies</a>. The first printing of <em>DOS for Dummies</em> was only 7,500 copies, giving no indication of what was to come for the series.</p>\n<p>When DOS gave way to Microsoft Windows, author Andy Rathbone released <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" product-id=\"1119470862\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1119470862/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1119470862\" target=\"_blank\" butter=\"butter\" nofollow=\"nofollow\" data-title=\"Windows 10 For Dummies (For Dummies (Computer/Tech))\" data-publisher=\"For Dummies\" data-releasedate=\"2018-05-22\" class=\"butter\">Windows for Dummies</a>, a title that would go on to sell more than 15 million copies, propelling it into the best-selling computer book of all time. Completely unrelated trivia that I couldn&#8217;t help but share: The character Mark &#8220;The Rat&#8221; Ratner in <em>Fast Times at Ridgemont High</em> is based on Rathbone. During Cameron Crowe&#8217;s research for the original book at Clairemont High School in San Diego, Rathbone and Crowe became friends. Rathbone would go on to publish 50 computer books.</p>\n<p>The Dummies series employed a winning formula: simple language and bold icons called attention to important pieces of information. The sections organized into &#8220;parts&#8221; grouped related chapters together. And the work of comic Rich Tennant was incorporated throughout to bring a little levity to the subject matter. At the end of each book, a section called &#8220;The Parts of Tens&#8221; would provide a list of ten items. These items would give further resources or interesting information not included in the rest of the book.</p>\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"alignleft size-large is-resized\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B0711CGR6Y/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=B0711CGR6Y\"><img src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/a-little-bit-of-everything-for-dummies-1.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-444249\" width=\"200\" srcset=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/a-little-bit-of-everything-for-dummies-1.jpg.optimal.jpg 318w, https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/a-little-bit-of-everything-for-dummies-1-240x300.jpg.optimal.jpg 240w, https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/a-little-bit-of-everything-for-dummies-1-300x375.jpg.optimal.jpg 300w, https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/a-little-bit-of-everything-for-dummies-1-40x50.jpg.optimal.jpg 40w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 318px) 100vw, 318px\" /></a></figure></div>\n<p>The series, while initially focused on things like creating webpages and writing HTML, decided in 1994 to branch out into more general interest topics. The first non-technology related book in the Dummies series was titled <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1119517893/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1119517893\" target=\"_blank\" product-id=\"1119517893\" butter=\"butter\" nofollow=\"nofollow\" data-title=\"Personal Finance For Dummies\" data-publisher=\"For Dummies\" data-releasedate=\"2018-11-13\" class=\"butter\">Personal Finance For Dummies</a> (and it remains the number one consumer title). Selling more than half a million copies, IDG realized it had a winner on its hands.&#160; They would go on to publish such titles as <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1119553008/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1119553008\" target=\"_blank\" product-id=\"1119553008\" butter=\"butter\" nofollow=\"nofollow\" data-title=\"Football For Dummies\" data-publisher=\"For Dummies\" data-releasedate=\"2019-06-12\" class=\"butter\">Football For Dummies</a>, <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0470767596/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0470767596\" target=\"_blank\" product-id=\"0470767596\" butter=\"butter\" nofollow=\"nofollow\" data-title=\"Fitness For Dummies\" data-publisher=\"For Dummies\" data-releasedate=\"2010-12-07\" class=\"butter\">Fitness For Dummies</a>, and <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0470106727/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0470106727\" target=\"_blank\" product-id=\"0470106727\" butter=\"butter\" nofollow=\"nofollow\" data-title=\"Etiquette For Dummies\" data-publisher=\"For Dummies\" data-releasedate=\"2007-06-05\" class=\"butter\">Etiquette For Dummies</a>, just to name a few. Some were more popular than others. <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" product-id=\"1119596564\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1119596564/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1119596564\" target=\"_blank\" butter=\"butter\" nofollow=\"nofollow\" data-title=\"Sex For Dummies\" data-publisher=\"For Dummies\" data-releasedate=\"2019-07-18\" class=\"butter\">Sex for Dummies</a>, a hugely popular title written by the famous Dr. Ruth Westheimer, was published in September 1995 to some pearl-clutching and couch-fainting.&#160; The more esoteric titles didn&#8217;t have quite the same sales numbers.  </p>\n<p>It&#8217;s a fun exercise to scroll through the over 2,500 Dummies titles published by IDG (and subsequently John Wiley &#38; Sons after their acquisition in 2001 of Hungry Minds, formerly IDG Books). You have books that land in the &#8220;You Probably Should Read Something More Than This Before Proceeding&#8221; category (<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1118603591/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1118603591\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Psychology for Dummies</em></a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0470039736/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0470039736\" target=\"_blank\"><em>IT Disaster Recovery Planning for Dummies</em></a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1119293464/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1119293464\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Chemistry for Dummies</em></a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0764576208/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0764576208\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Living With Hepatitis C for Dummies</em></a>), books that fall into the &#8220;Wow, This is Oddly Specific&#8221; category (<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0764552767/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0764552767\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Retired Racing Greyhounds for Dummies</em></a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1118871162/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1118871162\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Green Smoothies for Dummies</em></a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1118547543/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1118547543\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Gardening with Free-Range Chickens for Dummies</em></a>), and the &#8220;Eh, You Might As Well Get This Information Here&#8221; category (<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0470742593/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0470742593\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Flirting for Dummies</em></a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0470184086/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0470184086\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Conspiracy Theories &#38; Secret Societies for Dummies</em></a>, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0470039612/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0470039612\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Beagles for Dummies</em></a>).&#160;</p>\n<p>The Dummies series spawned a whole industry of books directed at the less-than-knowledgeable reader. While Dummies remained the gold standard, The Complete Idiot&#8217;s Guide from Alpha Books became a decent competitor (in fact, I&#8217;m pretty sure somewhere in this house is a copy of <em><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0028638840/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0028638840\" target=\"_blank\">The Complete Idiot&#8217;s Guide to Fishing</a>.</em> I have no idea why). Other series such as FabJob (how-to books for starting a business or career) and Teach Yourself (published by Hodder Headline) followed suit. Current publisher John Wiley &#38; Sons insists that they are unbothered by the competition, that there is room for all simplified reference books.</p>\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"alignleft size-large\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B0711CGR6Y/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=B0711CGR6Y\"><img src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/a-little-bit-of-everything-for-dummies-new-edition-1.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-444250\" srcset=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/a-little-bit-of-everything-for-dummies-new-edition-1.jpg.optimal.jpg 200w, https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/a-little-bit-of-everything-for-dummies-new-edition-1-40x50.jpg.optimal.jpg 40w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 200px) 100vw, 200px\" /></a></figure></div>\n<p>In Spring 2016, the Dummies series received a makeover. The dated cover art and typeface have made way for a slightly more sophisticated aesthetic. Tennant&#8217;s comic interludes were abandoned in 2012. These changes were clearly in an effort to gain the notice of readers in an environment where our attention is constantly divided.&#160; And how are they faring in a time when questions can be asked and answered within seconds? That remains to be seen. However, a quick browse on a subreddit page about the series leads me to believe that readers haven&#8217;t given up their beloved paper how-to books so easily. Many posters discuss the usefulness of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1119293359/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1119293359\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Guitars for Dummies</em></a> or <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0764551019/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0764551019\" target=\"_blank\"><em>Magic for Dummies</em></a> as something that, to this day, provide them with valuable, easy-to-reference information. And I&#8217;m sure it comes down to the topic. If you were to search for something like &#8220;Catholicism&#8221;, your Google results page would be met with both valid information, uninformed opinions, and conspiracies. And how does one wade through that conflicting information as someone entirely new to the topic? Is a book that is instructional and accessible a better format for a subject so fraught?</p>\n<p>The popular Dummies series would go on to see 200 million copies in approximately 2,500 titles translated into more than a dozen languages. It allowed readers more comfort in admitting they were ignorant on a topic and invited them to learn more. It was the gateway for information that employed no gatekeeper. The Dummies books were one of the precursors to having information at your fingertips. They may have spent the &#8217;90s and aughts being the brunt of sitcom jokes, but to the general public, they opened a door to a world of information.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Allen","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/a-little-bit-of-everything-for-dummies-1.jpg.optimal.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn43@2020_2/2020/08/31/08-20-39-952_efa9643477f45cc7.webp","https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/a-little-bit-of-everything-for-dummies-new-edition-1.jpg.optimal.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn59@2020_3/2020/08/31/08-19-42-918_db70d5df0e3dc5c6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/bookriot/WlRy?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn31@2020_6/2020/08/31/08-19-45-004_c8d434dfdd397063.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/bookriot/WlRy?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn80@2020_4/2020/08/31/08-19-42-637_bf7dfe7b4de90897.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/bookriot/WlRy?i=tcHwXkdeWlM:13ecEnPIvcg:oK5efhrsFR0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn43@2020_2/2020/08/31/08-19-45-244_c73ba568eb3fcad2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/bookriot/WlRy?i=tcHwXkdeWlM:13ecEnPIvcg:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn47@2020_6/2020/08/31/08-19-43-721_9be573e411d69365.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/bookriot/WlRy?d=ZC7T4KBF6Nw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn43@2020_6/2020/08/31/08-19-44-555_f5d09097629b39ce.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/bookriot/WlRy?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn11@2020_1/2020/08/31/08-19-44-808_6356ad1b69a203e9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/bookriot/WlRy/~4/tcHwXkdeWlM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn91@2020_4/2020/08/31/08-19-43-887_7c7d8f3f22a960e6.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598861981420},{"createdTime":"2020-08-31 16:19:41","updatedTime":"2020-08-31 16:19:41","title":"2020 Book Goal Updates","link":"https://bookriot.com/?p=443550","description":"\n<p>At the beginning of this year, <a href=\"https://bookriot.com/2020-book-goals/\">I wrote about my 2020 book goals</a>. Like everybody else, I looked at the start of a new year full of hope and optimism. I viewed this year as an opportunity to really challenge myself and not just in reading. I was going to really shine this year in my personal growth, my professional growth… </p>\n<p>Then March happened.  </p>\n<p>*cries in quarantine* </p>\n<p>We&#8217;re eight months into 2020 and no one expected this year to shape up the way it has. However sometimes you have to laugh through the tears! With that in mind, I decided to do a pulse check on my goals and how I’ve measured up so far. Yes, I know it’s technically no longer mid-year. I did intend to write this last month but (gestures wildly) life happened so here we are. Better late than never though, right?  </p>\n<p>One quick and serious call-out: I recognize that I’m fortunate to be able to focus enough to read. I know a lot of us really can’t right now. If you’re one of those, please don’t take this as a finger-wagging at you. If nothing else, 2020 has taught us that life is not a competition. Everyone is running in their own race and at their own pace. You have to do what is best for you and yours as well as your mental health.  </p>\n<p>And if anyone is saying there’s something wrong with you for not being able to focus on reading, put them out on the curb with the trash, be done with them, and be sure to thank your sanitation engineer if you see them. Who’s to say that my fanatical approach of keeping close track of what I’m reading on Goodreads and a spreadsheet is healthy? No one. I know that sitting in my own little corner, in my own little chair (cue music) works for me. It helps to give me a semblance of control in this otherwise hectic year, but it&#8217;s not the same for others.   </p>\n<p>That said, let’s get back to the humor and check in on my goals so far.</p>\n<h2>Fewer Books At Once</h2>\n<p>*laughs frantically* Oh yeah, this didn’t hold at all. It went straight out the window at the end of March when I started working from home and doing home schooling. I needed the distraction and sometimes I was just in a mood to start or read a different book. It helped the brain from worrying too much about the current state of not just my country but the world. Plus sometimes I would start a book and then need a break from the topic. It happens. I&#8217;ve fully embraced that I will likely always have a book harem.</p>\n<h2>More Audio Books</h2>\n<p>I was actually pleasantly surprised when I checked the numbers for this. So far in 2020, I have listened to a total of eight audio books. That’s an average of one per calendar month. This was especially impressive for me since I used to listen to my audio books while commuting to work. And, well, I’m not commuting currently. Technically, I started a total of ten but I stopped listening to three total (more on that later). There are other audiobooks I plan on reading before the end of the year is up as well. I am confident that I will surpass my number from last year. <br></p>\n<h2>Quality Not Quantity &#38; DNF More </h2>\n<p>I&#8217;m combining these two since they essentially fit hand in glove.  It may seem that I ignored this rule, based on the fact that I am reading more books at once, but that isn’t the case here. I’ve DNFed three books so far this year, two of which were audio. The first was a cozy mystery and by chapter five it was dragging and we still didn’t have a body. So away it went. Don’t @ me! Cozy or not, in a murder mystery I expect a body by chapter five or some sort of action. The second one was a cold case mystery, but again—roughly five chapters in, I just didn’t care. And the third one, which was actually a bummer, I just couldn’t get into in print. I plan on trying it later in audiobook form even if it isn’t this year. </p>\n<p>I won’t name books here since it&#8217;s not my style to discuss books I didn&#8217;t like or finish. Since I am DNFing without hesitation, I call these goals a win as well.  </p>\n<h2>Selective Reviews </h2>\n<p>I don’t think that I have done a lot of reviews this year; so I guess we’ll call this a win? If anything, I need to write more reviews. If nothing else, it will get me into the habit of writing more regularly.  </p>\n<h2>Read More Nonfiction about Women’s Contributions </h2>\n<p>I haven’t read a whole lot of nonfiction at all this year at all. I read a few graphic memoirs, but two of those were rereads. While they count in my overall numerical reading goal, I don&#8217;t personally count them for this goal. However, my book club did pick <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0590504932/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0590504932\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"The Cafeteria Lady from the Black Lagoon\" data-publisher=\"Scholastic\" data-releasedate=\"1998-09-01\" class=\"butter\">The Lady from the Black Lagoon</a> for this month&#8217;s pick, so there’s still hope! Although I’m not going to beat myself up too much for this. Reading about women’s contributions is great, but it can also be enraging, especially when you read about the chauvinism that women deal with daily now just as they did back then.</p>\n<h2>Finish One Previously Started Series </h2>\n<p>Nope! Haven’t even attempted this since I’ve been getting distracted by other books. But it’s only August, so I still have time. Due to how late in the year we are, it will likely be the <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0064471063/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0064471063\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"The Horse and His Boy\" data-publisher=\"HarperCollins\" data-releasedate=\"2002-03-05\" class=\"butter\">The Horse and His Boy</a> and <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0064471063/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0064471063\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"The Horse and His Boy\" data-publisher=\"HarperCollins\" data-releasedate=\"2002-03-05\" class=\"butter\">The Last Battle</a>, which are the final two in the <em>Chronicles of Narnia</em>. I’ve read the other five. Even if it has been years, it still counts!  </p>\n<p>And there it is. That’s my recap. Overall, I’m middlin’ to fair on my goals. Considering the rollercoaster of emotions that 2020 has been, I’m pleased with myself. There is still time to meet at least one or two of these goals and, if we&#8217;re lucky, for the year to turn around. If you have a reading milestone that you’re proud of, be sure to let us know over on social media! There&#8217;s not a scale or grading curve here. We’d love to cheer you on, since any achievement in 2020 is one worth cheering about.  </p>\n<p>And if your only reading goal for the year is to have more fun, <a href=\"https://bookriot.com/my-reading-goal/\">that&#8217;s okay too.</a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 16:19:41","updatedTime":"2020-08-31 16:19:41","title":"19 Black Feminist Books You Need In Your Library","link":"https://bookriot.com/?p=443780","description":"\n<p>I never realized the importance of Black feminist books and literature until I was an adult. I simply didn&#8217;t understand Black <a href=\"https://bookriot.com/best-feminist-books/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\"feminism (opens in a new tab)\">feminism</a> until I was much older. I believe my first introduction to Black feminism was Assata Shakur&#8217;s autobiography. Reading about her life and how she found political asylum in Cuba impacted me so much as a teen because I could not conceptualize having so much courage when everything and everyone is against you. </p>\n<p>When I watched <em>The Color Purple</em> as a young girl, I was traumatized but also it was a reminder that as a Black girl, my experiences as far different than white women and Black men. I suddenly found myself going down a rabbit hole of Black women writers who centered Black feminism in their works. Alice Walker, who coined the term womanism, gave me a better grasp of how Black women navigate and the language needed to express how I felt. </p>\n<p>When people ask me for a list of Black feminist reads, it&#8217;s almost an impossible task because there are just so many! So here I have listed a mix of fiction and nonfiction books, illustrated novels, and comics that are full of Black feminist thought, critiques, storytelling  and historical analysis. </p>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0812252381/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0812252381\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51aFaU6uXiL._SX328_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0812252381/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0812252381\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Wicked Flesh: Black Women, Intimacy, and Freedom in the Atlantic World (Early American Studies)\" data-publisher=\"University of Pennsylvania Press\" data-releasedate=\"2020-08-28\" class=\"butter\">Wicked Flesh: Black Women, Intimacy, and Freedom in the Atlantic World (Early American Studies)</a> by Jessica Marie Johnson</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Black womanhood and sexuality as it relates to feminism are typically discussed under the lens of how Black bodies are often sexualized and exploited. Johnson presents historical documents to illustrate the physiological and emotional impact slavery had on Black women from a reproductive point of view. Johnson also centers New Orleans as the epicenter of how Black women reclaimed their agency and embraced their sensuality. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0525560548/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0525560548\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51chQTmU2KL._SX329_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0525560548/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0525560548\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Hood Feminism: Notes from the Women That a Movement Forgot\" data-publisher=\"Viking\" data-releasedate=\"2020-02-25\" class=\"butter\">Hood Feminism: Notes from the Women That a Movement Forgot</a> by Mikki Kendall</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Poor Black women can be feminists, too. Even though their voices seem to get silenced in mainstream conversations, the impact of poor and working class Black women are often overlooked. They remain some of the biggest advocates and organizers and in this collection of essays, Kendall praises them. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1556520743/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1556520743\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51G3h0dXTVL._SX331_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1556520743/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1556520743\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Assata: An Autobiography\" data-publisher=\"Lawrence Hill Books\" data-releasedate=\"2001-11-01\" class=\"butter\">Assata: An Autobiography</a> by Assata Shakur</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>I read this book when I was a teen and it has stuck with me all these years. It&#8217;s a unique autobiography at a first-hand account of being a Black Panther as a Black woman. She details how she got involved in the movement as well as her experiences as being a Black woman revolutionary.</p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1888553855/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1888553855\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/41028ZRiR4L._SX353_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1888553855/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1888553855\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Letters to the Future: Black Women/Radical Writing\" data-publisher=\"Kore Press\" data-releasedate=\"2018-08-17\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Letters to the Future: Black Women/Radical Writing</a> by Erica Hunt (Editor), Dawn Lundy Martin (Editor) </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>A collection of writings and poems that centers not just cis het Black women but also Black LGBTQ+ people. The poems and essays include Black voices and experiences across generations and the African diaspora.</p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1324004614/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1324004614\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/41lO1JiVNIL._SX330_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1324004614/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1324004614\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"The Selected Works of Audre Lorde\" data-publisher=\"W. W. Norton &#38; Company\" data-releasedate=\"2020-09-08\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">The Selected Works of Audre Lorde</a> by Audre Lorde and Roxane Gay</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Audre Lorde is rightfully praised for her groundwork for Black feminism as a self-identified lesbian. This would make a great introduction for someone who is new to Lorde&#8217;s writing and work. Lorde&#8217;s Black queer theory is legendary amongst Black feminist scholars and readers. The book will be available on September 8, 2020.</p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0578502135/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0578502135\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51OyeKF7oL._SX322_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0578502135/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0578502135\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Black From the Future: A Collection of Black Speculative Writing\" data-publisher=\"Blf Press LLC\" data-releasedate=\"2019-08-20\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Black From the Future: A Collection of Black Speculative Writing</a> by Stephanie Andrea Allen (Author, Editor), Lauren Cherelle (Editor)</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Is there room in Afrofuturism for feminism? Of course there is. Looking in the future is where a lot of hope lies and for Black women that write sci-fi and speculative fiction, and dismantling patriarchy is not only possible in the future, it is required. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0807039829/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0807039829\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51ZQqU4AndL.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0807039829/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0807039829\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Unapologetic: A Black, Queer, and Feminist Mandate for Radical Movements\" data-publisher=\"Beacon Press\" data-releasedate=\"2019-08-27\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Unapologetic: A Black, Queer, and Feminist Mandate for Radical Movements</a> by Charlene Carruthers </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>If you need a crash course on how to be an intersectional Black feminist, this is a good crash course to fit in your bag if you are on the go. It&#8217;s straight to the point without any fluff and it centers Black queer women—who are more marginalized than cis het Black women.  </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0743476972/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0743476972\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51b1763IRcL._SX303_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0743476972/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0743476972\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"The Black Woman: An Anthology\" data-publisher=\"Washington Square Press\" data-releasedate=\"2005-03-29\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">The Black Woman: An Anthology</a> by Toni Cade Bambara and Eleanor W Traylor</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>This book was published in 1970 and it is remarkable how evergreen these essays remain. This book covers all topics including race, sex, politics, entertainment and the economy. No topic is left untouched. Read the works of Nikki Giovanni, Alice Walker, and more before they were known as bestselling authors and writers. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0679771263/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0679771263\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51LjQwprjnL._SX321_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0679771263/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0679771263\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Blues Legacies and Black Feminism: Gertrude &#34;Ma&#34; Rainey, Bessie Smith, and Billie Holiday\" data-publisher=\"Vintage\" data-releasedate=\"1999-01-26\" class=\"butter\">Blues Legacies and Black Feminism: Gertrude &#8220;Ma&#8221; Rainey, Bessie Smith, and Billie Holiday</a> by Angela Davis </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>You may not have thought about music, let alone Blues, as a feminist medium for Black women, but Dr. Angela Davis lays the framework on how these three Black women used Blues to voice their radical sentiments on Black womanhood. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0593099605/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0593099605\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51LK0FHKp3L.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0593099605/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0593099605\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"The Year of the Witching\" data-publisher=\"Ace\" data-releasedate=\"2020-07-21\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">The Year of the Witching</a> by Alexis Henderson</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>I can&#8217;t believe I found out about this book on Twitter. This book is for people who love dark fantasy books, witches, and occult stories with a feminist tone. It centers Immanuelle Moore who tries to follow the law of the land. However, she finds herself learning of her mother&#8217;s life and how it ties to witches and makes it her mission to undo all the wrong the Church in Bethel has done. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1629634484/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1629634484\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51xr0y1SgoL._SX348_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1629634484/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1629634484\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"(H)afrocentric Comics: Volumes 1–4\" data-publisher=\"PM Press\" data-releasedate=\"2017-09-01\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">(H)afrocentric Comics: Volumes 1–4</a> by Juliana &#8220;Jewels&#8221; Smith (Author), Mike Hampton (Illustrator), Ronald Nelson (Illustrator), Kiese Laymon (Foreword)</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>There aren&#8217;t a lot of Black feminist comics, however, <em>(H)Afrocentric</em> does a great job in illustrating what radical social justice movements entail. Enjoy the illustrations of a story that paints a picture of how Black women and other people of color fight gentrification in their neighborhood and local campus. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0692901930/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0692901930\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51dsucqd7yL._SX331_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0692901930/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0692901930\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"The Keepers: Origins\" data-publisher=\"Aza Entertainment\" data-releasedate=\"2017-04-30\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">The Keepers: Origins</a> by by Jazmin Truesdale and (Author), Remero Colston (Illustrator)</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Truesdale has created an entire universe of women characters that are superheroes. In this illustrated space opera adventure, women are selected to be the keepers of their universe. This is a book for all ages, especially younger readers who need to see more representation of themselves. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1400033438/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1400033438\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/41M1raVXSjL._SX322_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1400033438/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1400033438\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Sula\" data-publisher=\"Vintage\" data-releasedate=\"2004-06-08\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Sula</a> By Toni Morrison </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p><em>Sula</em> examines Black feminism on how women treat each other in platonic relationships, especially when you involve men. This book is both a drama and a slight horror story on how intra-community dynamics can be just as harmful as navigating mainstream society. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0451531787/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0451531787\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51DTAskjqCL._SX303_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0451531787/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0451531787\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"To Be Young, Gifted and Black (Signet Classics)\" data-publisher=\"Signet\" data-releasedate=\"2011-01-04\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">To Be Young, Gifted and Black</a> By Lorraine Hansberry</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Hanberry became the first Black woman playwright to have a play on Broadway for <em>A Raisin in the Sun</em>, but her autobiography paints her life as an ambitious queer Black creative from Chicago. In her book, she talks about how she navigates Blackness with her sexuality and art. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1936932733/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1936932733\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/41iF2MgUKIL._SX332_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1936932733/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1936932733\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"I Love Myself When I Am Laughing... And Then Again When I Am Looking Mean and Impressive: A Zora Neale Hurston Reader\" data-publisher=\"The Feminist Press at CUNY\" data-releasedate=\"2020-01-07\" class=\"butter\">I Love Myself When I Am Laughing…And Then Again When I Am Looking Mean and Impressive: A Zora Neale Hurston Reader</a> by Zora Neale Hurston</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Hurston, a writer, visionary, and anthropologist, wrote in African American Vernacular English (AAVE) in a lot of her works. She highlighted southern Black life as a culture that was often forgotten when it came to Black America. This is book that combines Black folk art storytelling and feminism. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1951491009/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1951491009\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/51kt1S8lu4L._SX307_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1951491009/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1951491009\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Stupid Black Girl: Essays from an American African\" data-publisher=\"Street Noise Books\" data-releasedate=\"2020-06-30\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Stupid Black Girl: Essays from an American African</a> by Aisha Redux (Author), Brianna McCarthy (Illustrator)</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>There is no one way of being Black, and being Black as a first generation American can be a uniquely different experience altogether. Redux talks about a variety of topics such as gentrification to their personal experience with the September 11 tragedy. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0156028646/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0156028646\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/4191e-LlHsL._SX341_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0156028646/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0156028646\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"In Search of Our Mothers' Gardens: Womanist Prose\" data-publisher=\"Mariner Books\" data-releasedate=\"2003-05-19\" class=\"butter\">In Search of Our Mothers&#8217; Gardens: Womanist Prose</a> By Alice Walker </h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Walker created the term womanism which means Black feminism and is meant to center Black women&#8217;s experience, because white feminism does not. In this collection of essays, Walker relives her experiences and recounts of the Civil Rights Movement under the scope of Black womanism thought.  </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0996891064/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0996891064\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/41cGycXaebL._SX331_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0996891064/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0996891064\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Young Revolutionary: A Teen's Guide to Activism\" data-publisher=\"Literary Revolutionary, The\" data-releasedate=\"2018-02-17\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Young Revolutionary: A Teen&#8217;s Guide to Activism</a> by Chanice Lee</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>When I was a teen, I would have loved to have had the chance to read about other Black teen girls and how they are making waves to have a progressive future. This guide is perfectly executed as teens give their experiences on how they became activists and what they seeking to change. </p></div></div></div>\n<div class=\"wp-block-book-blurb-block-main bookblurb-block\"><div class=\"card__content\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0983839867/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0983839867\"><img class=\"bookblurb__image\" src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/41mycuxtpqL._SX331_BO1204203200_.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" aria-hidden=\"true\"/></a><h3 class=\"bookblurb__booktitle\"><a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0983839867/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0983839867\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Unf*uckablewith: Rising From The Ashes Into Your Black Woman Badassery\" data-publisher=\"Catriceology Enterprises\" data-releasedate=\"2019-02-15\" class=\"butter\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Unf*uckablewith: Rising From The Ashes Into Your Black Woman Badassery</a> by Catrice M. Jackson</h3><div class=\"bookblurb__description\"><p>Sometimes we just need to sit and think about the women who came before us. Jackson gives us a bold and unapologetic self-help guide that&#8217;s also a memoir on Black feminism, self-care and being resilient when the odds are against you.  </p></div></div></div>\n<div 16:19:41","updatedTime":"2020-08-31 16:19:41","title":"6 British YA Authors of Color for Your To-Be-Read List","link":"https://bookriot.com/?p=441122","description":"\n<p>Over the years &#8211; especially recent ones &#8211; there have been many necessary conversations about the importance of increased representation in the U.S. publishing industry. Readers deserve to see themselves in the stories told and to be able to identify with the authors writing those books. This also extends to the diversity of publishing industry professionals. Progress has been made, but more needs to be done. And this is an issue that&#8217;s not specific just to the U.S. </p>\n<p>There&#8217;s also a lack of diversity and inclusion in publishing in the United Kingdom, Britain included. <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/books/2019/jan/16/publishers-failing-to-improve-racial-and-regional-diversity-survey-finds\">The Guardian reported</a> on a survey in 2019 that showed publishers aren&#8217;t doing enough to &#8220;improve the racial and regional diversity of the publishing workforce.&#8221; </p>\n<p>Keep in mind that there are contemporary authors from the region doing great work, and there are different ways to work towards increased representation. One way that readers can make a difference is by reading diversely &#8211; not only does this show the industry that minorities authors have reader support, you&#8217;ll get to enjoy a lot of good books that are worth reading. </p>\n<p>Consider adding books by the following six British authors of color to your to-be-read list, if you haven&#8217;t already. I&#8217;m adding books to my list too. </p>\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"alignleft size-large is-resized\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Noughts-Crosses-and/dp/0241324076/ref=tmm_pap_swatch_0?_encoding=UTF8&#38;qid=1595776566&#38;sr=8-2\"><img src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Noughts-Crosses-Book-Cover.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-441152\" width=\"200\" srcset=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Noughts-Crosses-Book-Cover.jpg.optimal.jpg 318w, https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Noughts-Crosses-Book-Cover-196x300.jpg.optimal.jpg 196w, https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Noughts-Crosses-Book-Cover-245x375.jpg.optimal.jpg 245w, https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Noughts-Crosses-Book-Cover-33x50.jpg.optimal.jpg 33w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 318px) 100vw, 318px\" /></a></figure></div>\n<h3>Malorie Blackman</h3>\n<p>Writing since her late 20s, Malorie Blackman has written children&#8217;s books, for television, and for the stage, <a href=\"https://literature.britishcouncil.org/writer/malorie-blackman\">according to the British Council</a>. Thus far, she has had <a href=\"https://www.malorieblackman.co.uk/qa-with-malorie/\">69 books published</a>. In 2008, Blackman was appointed an OBE, and from 2013 to 2015 she was the Children&#8217;s Laureate. She has also received a variety of other awards for her writing. </p>\n<p>The Noughts and Crosses YA series includes: <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1416900160/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1416900160\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Naughts &#38; Crosses\" data-publisher=\"Simon &#38; Schuster Books for Young Readers\" data-releasedate=\"2005-06-01\" class=\"butter\">Noughts &#38; Crosses</a>,<a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1416900187/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=1416900187\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Knife Edge\" data-publisher=\"Simon &#38; Schuster Books for Young Readers\" data-releasedate=\"2007-07-24\" class=\"butter\"> Knife Edge</a>, <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0141378662/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0141378662\" class=\"butter\">Checkmate</a>, <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0141378670/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0141378670\" class=\"butter\">Double Cross</a>, <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0241388449/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0241388449\" class=\"butter\">Crossfire</a>, and <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0241388791/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0241388791\" class=\"butter\">Nought Forever</a>. Noughts and Crosses was adapted for the screen by the BBC. In addition, Blackman has <a href=\"https://www.malorieblackman.co.uk/category/books/\">written more YA books</a> like <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0141377011/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0141377011\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Chasing The Stars\" data-publisher=\"PUFFIN\" data-releasedate=\"2017-04-06\" class=\"butter\">Chasing the Stars</a>. </p>\n<p>Check out this <a href=\"https://bookriot.com/why-we-need-noughts-and-crosses-and-its-upcoming-adaptation/\">Book Riot article on why Noughts and Crosses and its adaptation are needed</a>. </p>\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"alignleft size-large is-resized\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B078W6CK51/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i6\"><img src=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Crongton-Knights-Book-Cover.jpg.optimal.jpg\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-441153\" width=\"200\" srcset=\"https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Crongton-Knights-Book-Cover.jpg.optimal.jpg 310w, https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Crongton-Knights-Book-Cover-186x300.jpg.optimal.jpg 186w, https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Crongton-Knights-Book-Cover-233x375.jpg.optimal.jpg 233w, https://s2982.pcdn.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Crongton-Knights-Book-Cover-31x50.jpg.optimal.jpg 31w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 310px) 100vw, 310px\" /></a></figure></div>\n<h3>Alex Wheatle </h3>\n<p>So far, Alex Wheatle&#8217;s <a href=\"https://literature.britishcouncil.org/writer/alex-wheatle\">literary achievements include</a>: being named an MBE; being shortlisted for the Carnegie Medal in 2016; and the YA Book Prize in 2018. Wheatle is also on the shortlist for the 2021 NSK Neustadt Prize for Children&#8217;s Literature, <a href=\"https://www.neustadtprize.org/shortlist-for-the-2021-nsk-neustadt-prize-for-childrens-literature-announced/\">per an official announcement</a>. </p>\n<p>Interested in reading some of Wheatle&#8217;s books? Look no further. Among his works is the Crongton series (<a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0349001995/ref=as_li_tf_il?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=boorio-20&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;camp=217145&#38;creative=399349&#38;creativeASIN=0349001995\" target=\"_blank\" data-title=\"Liccle Bit (Crongton)\" data-publisher=\"Atom\" data-releasedate=\"2018-03-27\" class=\"butter\">Liccle Bit</a>, <a title=\"Buy from Amazon\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"
